That pasta is simply inedible... and the washbasin in the room, which looks good with its shallow surface, but is really not easy to use. Then the most unsatisfactory thing is the restaurant in the style of the Republic of China. When I took the elderly to visit, the waitress was on guard. When I wanted to go upstairs, I ran over and said that the upstairs was a private room and was not open to the public. It's just a restaurant, so what? My good impression of the hotel service was instantly lowered.
Then let's talk about the advantages: the biggest advantage is of course the geographical location. It is at the innermost of Yunqi Bamboo Path, surrounded by bamboo forests and ancient trees and greenery. It is estimated that in autumn, the mountains will be covered with red maples, which is more suitable for quiet leisure (some tour groups will indeed be very annoying). There are two trails up and down the mountain. The one with wooden plank roads is quieter and more suitable for walking. The hotel is not far from Meijiawu, and it takes more than ten or twenty minutes to walk there, which is very convenient. The large fish tank in the hotel lobby is also very distinctive, but it is a bit out of place in such a hotel hidden in the forest.

The hotel is based on black and white, Hui style tones; the restaurant, the Republic of China Courtyard, is of excellent quality, except for the large portion, which may not be good for one person. The small cakes for afternoon tea are also pretty good.
It rained for two days and I almost didn't go out. The hotel is located in the Yunqi Bamboo Trail Scenic Area. It's a quiet path and I feel relaxed and happy even after taking two steps. On the way up and down the mountain, I can remember the sense of freedom of wandering in the bamboo forest for a long time.
